3 (623)
Indra (1тАУ20), Pa╠Дkastha╠Дman Kauraya╠Дn╠гaтАЩs Da╠Дnastuti (21тАУ24)
Medhy─Бtithi K─Бс╣Зva
24 verses: br╠еhat─л alternating with satobr╠еhat─л, 1тАУ20, arranged in prag─Бthas, anuс╣гс╣нubh 12, g─Бyatr─л 22тАУ23, br╠еhat─л 24
Like the previous two hymns, this one consists of a long praise of Indra (vss. 1тАУ20) followed by a short d─Бnastuti (21тАУ24). The Indra portion is arranged in stan dard prag─Бthas, while the d─Бnastuti is metrically more varied. The verse pairs of the prag─Бthas are for the most part internally unified, but like many of the longer hymns in VIII there is not much apparent structure in the hymn as a whole. There are, however, several recurrent themes: the greatness (mahim├бn) and vast power (┼Ы├бvas) of Indra (e.g., vss. 4, 6); the gods and poets who have previously celebrated Indra and have been helped by him (e.g., vss. 7тАУ9, 16); and the sheer noise made by IndraтАЩs praisers (e.g., vss. 3, 7, 16, 18). In the context of all this previous poetic activity, verses 13 and 14 raise anxious questions about what constitutes the proper topic of praise poetry and how to configure these praises anew, the perennial prob
lem of the R╠еgvedic bard.
The d─Бnastuti is far easier to interpret than those of the previous two hymns: the patron P─Бkasth─Бman is celebrated for his gift of a particularly fine sorrel horse, given also by Indra and the Maruts. The first half of the last verse (24) seems to contain an adage, or adapted piece of folk wisdom, as a foil to further praise of the patron in the second half of the verse. The verse itself has a slight Pindaric ring.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬDrink, Indra, of our sapid libation, mixed with milk, and be satisfied; regard thyself as our kinsman, to beexhilarated along with us for our welfare; may your (good) intentions protect us.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

As our kinsman: or, as ourkinsman, to be exhilarated along with us, think for our welfare; this с╣Ыca and с╣Ыcas 2-20 are used as a prag─Бtha

+Jamison Brereton

Drink of the sap-filled pressed (soma). Reach exhilaration from our (soma) accompanied by cows, Indra.
Become a friend, a feasting companion, for our strengthening. Let your insights help us.

+Griffith

DRINK, Indra, of the savoury juice, and cheer thee with our milky draught.
Be, for our weal, our Friend and sharer of the feast, and let thy wisdom guard us well.

+Geldner

Trink vom w├╝rzigen, berausche dich, Indra, an unserem milchgemischten Saft! Sei du der Freund und Zechgenosse uns zum Gedeihen! Deine Absichten sollen uns g├╝nstig sein!

+Grassmann

O Indra, trink den saft’gen Trank, berausch am milchgemischten dich; Sei uns zum Heil, Genosse bei dem Opferschmaus, es f├╢rdre deine Einsicht uns.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬMay we be offerers of oblations (to enjoy) your favour; harm us not for the sake of the enemy; protectus with your wondrous solicited (protections), maintain us ever in felicity.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

We would be in the good favor of you, the prizewinner. Do not lay us low before hostility.
Help us with your conspicuous powers to prevail. Keep us in your good thoughts.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

I am not sure why the тАЬfuture imperativeтАЭ avat─Бt is used in p─Бda c. Its use implies that Indra should, first, not lay us low and, then, actually help us. This is possible but not compellingly required by the sense.

+Griffith

In thy kind grace and favour may we still be strong: expose us not to foe’s attack.
With manifold assistance guard and succour us, and bring us to felicity.

+Geldner

Wir wollen in deiner, des Siegreichen, Gunst stehen. Wirf uns nicht dem Feinde hin! Steh uns mit deiner wunderbaren ├Ьbermacht bei; befestige uns in deiner Gande!

+Grassmann

In deiner Gnade seien reichgesegnet wir, nicht wirf uns dem Verfolger hin; Mit mannichfacher H├╝lfeleistung f├╢rdre uns, und nimm uns auf in deine Gunst.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬIndra, by the might of his strength, has spread out the heaven and earth; Indra has lighted up the sun;in Indra are all beings aggregated; the distilling drops of the Soma flow to Indra.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Indra has lighted up the suс╣ЕIndra restores the sun from the grasp of svarbh─Бnu, extricates him from eclipse

+Jamison Brereton

Indra by his greatness spread the two worlds and his vast power; Indra made the sun shine.
Within Indra are all beings held and within Indra the pressed drops.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

P─Бda-final ┼Ы├бvaс╕е here is often considered to stand for instr. ┼Ы├бvas─Б (see Oldenberg for previous lit., GeldnerтАЩs tr. and n., and most recently Hale [Fs. Melchert], who takes it as an archaic zero-grade s-stem instr., with loss of laryngeal in pause; see comm. ad VIII.39.2). However, as Oldenberg points out, an accusative reading is perfectly possible.

The presence of the same p─Бda-final nom.-acc. form nearby (4c, 8a, 10b) supports an accusative interpretation here.

+Griffith

With might hath Indra spread out heaven and earth, with power hath Indra lighted up the Sun.
In Indra are all creatures closely held; in him meet the distilling Soma-drops.

+Geldner

Indra hat durch seine Macht, durch seine St├дrke beide Welten ausgebreitet; Indra lie├Я die Sonne leuchten. Dem Indra haben sich alle Welten, dem Indra die ausgepre├Яten S├дfte zu eigen gegeben.

+Grassmann

Zur Kraft hat Indra Erd’ und Himmel ausgedehnt und Indra hat die Sonn’ erhellt; Allein zu Indra streben alle Wesen hin, zu Indra der gepresste Saft.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬMen glorify you, Indra, with hymns that you may drink the first (of the gods); the associated с╣Ъbhusunite in your praise, the Rudras glorify the ancient (Indra).тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

To you, for you to drink first, o Indra, with their praises the ─Аyus and the R╠еbhus united sounded together, and the Rudras sang (to you) as the foremost.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The p┼лrv├б- in p┼лrv├бp─лtaye ushers in a set of verses with p┼лrva- forms (7d, 8d, 9b, 11d).

+Griffith

Men with their lauds are urging thee, Indra, to drink the Soma first.
The Rbhus in accord have lifted up their voice, and Rudras sung thee as the first.

+Geldner

Dich. Indra, riefen zum ersten Trunk die Ayu┬┤s mit Lobliedern, riefen vereint die Ribhu┬┤s an, priesen die Rudra┬┤s als Ersten.

+Grassmann

Mit Lobges├дngen rauschen dir die Menschen zu beim ersten Trunk; Im Chore singt die Ribhuschar dem ewigen, die Rudraschar verherrlicht ihn.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬIndra augments the energy and the strength of this (his worshipper), when he exhilaration of the Somais diffused through his body; men celebrate in due order his might today as they did of old.тАЭ

Viс╣гс╣Зavi: an epithet of made:┼Ыar─лravy─Бpake, diffused through the body; or, may be an equivalent of yaj├▒a, at sacrifice

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬWherewith you have sent the great waters tot he ocean; such as is your wish-fulfilling strength; thatmight of Indra is not easily to be resisted which the earth obeys.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Such is your wish-fulfilling: or, that your strengthwherewith… is wish-fulfilling

+Jamison Brereton

With which you sent the great waters surging to the sea, that is your bullish vast power, Indra.
In a single day that greatness of his cannot be fully attained, toward which the battle-cry has roared.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

For vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гс╣Зi and the phrase vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гс╣Зi te ┼Ы├бvaс╕е see disc. ad VIII.96.19.

Thieme (KZ 92: 46) rejects the usual interpr. of kс╣гon─л╠Бс╕е as nom. sg., on the grounds that the nom. sg. is attested as kс╣гoс╣З─л╠Бin I.180.5 and that kс╣гoс╣З─л╠Бс╕е is otherwise nom. or acc. pl. However, this requires him to interpr. it as an acc. pl. of Inhalts or result with a passive verb: тАЬdem (d.h.: wenn ihm) Gebr├╝ll (aufr├╝ttelndes Kampfgechrei) hinterhergeschreien worden ist.тАЭ The syntactic complications of this interpr. seem to me to outweigh the drawbacks of assuming that the poorly attested stem kс╣гoс╣З─л╠Б- could generate a nom. sg. in -─л╠Бs, esp. since its suffixal accent matches that of vс╣Ыk─л╠Б-type nouns.

+Griffith

Wherewith thou sentest mighty waters to the sea, that, Indra, is thy manly strength.
For ever unattainable is this power of him to whom the worlds have cried aloud.

+Geldner

Das, Indra, ist deine Bullenkraft, mit welcher du die gro├Яen Gew├дsser zum Meere laufen lie├Яest. Nicht an einem Tage ist diese seine Macht zu erreichen, hinter dem seine Heerschar herbr├╝llte.

+Grassmann

Die Manneskraft, mit der du, Indra, in das Meer der Wasser Schwall ergossen hast, Erreichet niemand, noch auch dessen Gr├╢sse je, dem Wasserflut entgegenrauscht.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬGrant us, Indra, the wealth accompanied by vigour, which I solicit from you; give (wealth) first of all tohim desirous of gratifying you, presenting (sacrificial) food; give (wealth), you who are of old, to him who glorifiesyou.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Muster your ability for us, Indra, when I beg you for wealth and a mass of good heroes.
Muster your ability for the one striving to first win the prize. Muster your ability for the praise song, foremost one.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Rather than construing v─Б╠Бj─Бya directly with ┼Ыagdh├н, as Geldner does (тАЬTu uns, was du kannst zum SiegerpreisтАжтАЭ), I interpret it as the object of the participle s├нс╣г─Бsate, attracted into the dative in the fashion of datival phrases like vс╣Ыtr─Б╠Бya h├бntave (e.g., III.37.5-6). For the VP see VIII.103.11 v─Б╠Бjaс╣Г s├нс╣г─Бsataс╕е. However, 12d ┼Ыagdh├н st├│m─Бya may support GeldnerтАЩs interpretation.

+Griffith

Help us, O Indra, when we pray to thee for wealth and hero might.
First help thou on to strength the man who strives to win, and aid our laud, O Ancient One.

+Geldner

Tu f├╝r uns, was du kannst, Indra, da ich dich um Reichtum, um die Meisterschaft bitte! Tu, was du kannst zum Siegerpreis f├╝r den, der den ersten zu gewinnen trachtet; tu, was du kannst, zu unserem Loblied, du Allererster!

+Grassmann

Sei hold uns, Indra, wenn ich dich um Reichthum bitt’ und Heldenkraft, Verhilf zu Labung dem, der sie zuerst begehrt, sei hold dem Loblied, ewiger.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬGive to this our (worshipper) engaged in celebrating your sacred rites, Indra, (the wealth) whereby youhave protected the son of Puru, grant to the man (aspiring) to heaven (the wealth wherewith) you havepreserved, O Indra, Ru┼Ыama, ┼Ъy─Бvaka and Kс╣Ыpa.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Muster your ability for us since you helped Paura (and help) the insights of this one striving to win, Indra.
Muster your ability just as you furthered Ru┼Ыama, ┼Ъy─Бvaka, and Kr╠еpa possessing solar glory, Indra.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

GeldnerтАЩs interpretation of ab (тАЬTu uns, was du kannst, f├╝r diesen, der [den Preis] der Dichtung gewinnen m├╢chte, da du ja dem Paura beigestanden hastтАЭ) is syntactically quite troublesome, in that it not only involves an embedded relative (rare to non-existent in the RV) y├бd тАж ─Б╠Бvitha, but one that splits up a close constituent asy├б … s├нс╣г─Бsataс╕е. Oldenberg, by contrast, takes dh├нyaс╕е as object of ─Б╠Бvitha parallel to paur├бm and cites abundant parallels for тИЪav + dh├нyam, -aс╕е. This allows the y├бd clause to be normally positioned, although I still find the position of the asy├б unusual. I also supply a presential form of тИЪav to govern dh├нyaс╕е, since the aid to the striverтАЩs insights seems to be a matter of current concern.

Unlike Geldner I do not take sv├аrс╣Зaram as a fourth client of IndraтАЩs, but as an epithet of the final name in a classic BehagelтАЩs Law construction. In the next hymn (VIII.4.2) mentioning Ru┼Ыama, ┼Ъy─Бvaka, and Kr╠еpa there is no Svarс╣Зara. I also take it as an epithet in VIII.12.2, but as a PN in VIII.6.39.

+Griffith

Help for us, Indra, as thou holpest Paura once, this man’s devotions bent on gain.
Help, as thou gavest Rugama and Syavaka and Svarnara and Krpa aid.

+Geldner

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬWhat living mortal, the prompter of ever-rising (praises), may now glorify Indra? No one of thoseheretofore praising him have attained the greatness of the properties of Indra.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

What among the unshakable things should a powerful mortal sing anew?
For, (even though) singing the sun, they have not reached his greatness, his Indrian power.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

It is generally, and reasonably, accepted (e.g., Grassmann, Oldenberg, EWA s.v. atas─л╠Б-) that the hapax atas─л╠Бn─Бm belongs with atas─Б╠Бyya-, attested twice, so its meaning depends on our interpretation of the latter - generally held to mean тАШto be called/praisedтАЩ. However, I take atas─Б╠Бyya as a negated gerundive to тИЪtaс╣Гs тАШshakeтАЩ (see I.63.6), and so atas─л╠Б- should mean тАШunshakeable, unshaking, firmтАЩ. In context here, I assume that it refers to the stable, fixed elements of the cosmic world and the standard subjects of poetry. This may implicitly contrast with n├бvyaс╕е тАШanewтАЩ, sketching the usual tension between the poetтАЩs desire to produce a new song and the fact that his topics are preordained.

This category of possible atas─л╠Бpoetic topics is then exemplified by the sun in p─Бda d тАФ a subject that, despite its greatness, does not match the greatness of Indra.

This interpretation of cd follows Oldenberg; Geldner switches the objects of participle and main verb, taking sv├аr with ─Бna┼Ыuс╕е and mahim─Б╠Бnam with gс╣Ыс╣З├бntaс╕е: тАЬDenn noch nicht haben die, welchen seine indrische Gr├╢sse besingen, die Sonne erreicht.тАЭ Although word order is hardly a reliable guide to RVic interpretation, the adjacency of p─Бdainitial sv├аr gс╣Ыс╣З├бntaс╕е weakly favors the Oldenberg interpretation, which also makes more sense.

+Griffith

What newest of imploring prayers shall, then, the zealous mortal sing?
For have not they who laud his might, and Indra-power won for themselves the light of heaven?

+Geldner

Was k├╢nnte ein Sterblicher, der es anderen zuvortut, neues an Bittgebeten singen? Denn noch nicht haben die, welche seine indrische Gr├╢├Яe besingen, die Sonne erreicht.

+Grassmann

Welch neues Lob soll bringen ihm der schnelle Mensch im Bettlerschwarm? Denn nie ermessen seine Indragr├╢sse die, die preisen seinen Himmelsglanz.

+Elizarenkova

тАЬWho, praising you as the deity, (ever) hoped to sacrifice to you? What saint, what sage conveys (hispraises to yo?) When, opulent Indra, have you come to the invocation of one pouring out libations, of onerepeating (your) praise?тАЭ

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThese most sweet songs, these hymns of praise ascent (to you), like triumphant chariots laden withwealth, charged with unfailing protections, intended to procure food.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Like triumphant chariots: v─Бjayantahannam icchanto rath─Б iva, though the epithets are plural masc., yet, they agree with rath─Бс╕е

+Jamison Brereton

These most honeyed songs and praises rise upтАФ
entirely victorious, gaining the stake, possessing imperishable help, competing for the prize like chariots.

+Griffith

These songs of ours exceeding sweet, these hymns of praise ascend to thee,
Like ever-conquering chariots that display their strength, gain wealth, and give unfailing aid.

тАЬThe Bhс╣Ыgus, like the Kaс╣Зvas, have verily attained to the all- pervading (Indra), on whom they havemeditated, as the sun (pervades the unverse by his rays); men of the Priyamedha race, worshipping Indra withpraises glorify him.тАЭ

+Griffith

The Bhrgus are like Suns, like Kanvas, and have gained all that their thoughts were bent upon.
The living men of Priyamedha’s race have sung exalting Indra with their lauds.

I.48.7 eс╣г─Б╠Бyukta par─Бv├бtaс╕е, s┼л╠Бryasyod├бyan─Бd ├бdhi тАЬThis one has hitched herself up from out of the distance, from (the place of) the rising of the sunтАЭ (also I.115.4, V.87.4, VII.60.3, 75.4, X.94.12, etc.).

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThese wise celebrators (of holy rites) repeatedly propitiate you with pious praise for the acceptance ofthe sacrifice; do you, opulent Indra, who are entitled to praise, hear our invocation like one who listens to what hedesires.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Veno na (from vena, k─Бnti-karm─Б), yath─Б j─Бt─Бbhil─Бс╣гaс╕е puruс╣гaс╕е k─Бmayitavyam aik─Бgryeс╣Зa┼Ыс╣Ыс╣Зoti, as a man full of desire listens attentively to that which is agreeable

+Jamison Brereton

For these bards, inspired poets, have bellowed for you for the winning of wisdom with their insight.
You, o bounteous Indra longing for songsтАФlike a tracker listen to our call.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Most assign v─Бva┼Ы├║с╕е to тИЪva┼Ы тАШdesireтАЩ (e.g., Geldner тАЬdiese deine Dichter тАж verlangenтАжтАЭ; so also Grassmann, Lubotsky), but I take it to тИЪv─Б┼Ы тАШbellowтАЩ. K├╝mmel (477-80) allows both possibilities, though he argues that the original affiliation of the pf. stem v─Бva┼Ыwas to тИЪv─Б┼Ы, though it may have become partially co-opted by тИЪva┼Ы by semantic overlap. I have opted for тИЪv─Б┼Ы because this hymn contains a number of instances of noise-making by poets or their substitutes: 3d abh├н тАж an┼лс╣гata, 7c s├бm asvaran, 16d asvaran, in addition to the usual verbs of singing and praising. Notice also the very parallel 5cd … hav─Бmahe … dh├бnasya s─Бt├бye, with a verb of calling and X s─Бt├бye.

+Griffith

For these, the bards and singers, have cried out to thee with prayer, to gain the sacrifice.
As such, O Maghavan, Indra, who lovest song, even as a lover bear my call.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬWhen you had expelled the mighty Ahi from the firmament, then the fires blazed out, the sun shoneforth, the ambrosial Soma destined for Indra flowed out, and you, Indra, did manifest your manhood.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

The fires shone out, out the sun, out the soma, the Indrian sap.
You blew the great serpent out from the midspace: that manly act did you perform, Indra.

+Griffith

Bright were the flaming fires, the Sun gave forth his shine, and Soma, Indra’s juice, shone clear.
Indra, thou blewest the great Dragon from the air -. men must regard that valorous deed.

+Geldner

Die Feuer kamen gl├дnzend zum Vorschein, und die Sonne, und Soma, der indrische Saft kam zum Vorschein. Aus dem Luftraum bliesest du hinweg den gro├Яen Drachen: Diese Mannestat hast du vollbracht, Indra.

+Grassmann

Es leuchteten die Feuer auf, der Sonne Glanz, der Somasaft, des Indra Trank; Du bliesest weg die grosse Schlange aus der Luft, dies Manneswerk hast du vollbracht.

+Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬSuch wealth as Indra and the Maruts have bestowed upon me, such has P─Бkasth─Бman, the son ofKuray─Бс╣Зa, bestowed, of itself the most magnificent of all, like the quick-moving (sun) in the sky.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

The one that Indra and the Maruts, that P─Бkasth─Бman, the son of Kuray─Бс╣Зa, gave meтАФ
the most beautiful of all in body, like the one that runs in heaven
[=sun]тАФ

home, like birds the son of Tugra.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The son of Tugra is Bhujyu, a client of the A┼Ыvins, whom they rescue with birds or winged steeds - a tale alluded to especially in the Kakс╣г─лvant hymns (e.g., I.116.3-5, 117.14).

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬHis father’s own son, the giver of dwellings, the sustainer of strength like (invigorating) unguents, Icelebrate P─Бkasth─Бman, the destroyer (of foes), the despoiler (of enemies), the donor of the tawny (horse).тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Food is the lifebreath, garments the body, and anointment is the giver of strength.
But as the fourth I have proclaimed P─Бkasth─Бman, the nurturing giver of the sorrel.

+Griffith

Raiment is body, food is life, and healing ointment giveth strength.
As the free-handed giver of the ruddy steed, I have named Pakasthaman fourth.

+Geldner

Speise ist die Seele, Kleidung der K├╢rper, Salb├╢l ist kraftverleihend. Als Vierten habe ich den gastfreien Pakasthaman, den Verschenker des roten Rosses genannt.

+Grassmann

Lebenshauch ist der [geschenkte] Trank, ein Leib das Kleid, und Kraft der geschenkte Schmuck; als den vierten freigiebigen Schenker des rothen Rosses nannte ich den P─Бkasth─Бman.

+Elizarenkova
